<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg/220px-Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg/330px-Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg/440px-Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1176" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a> Research Center, Aachen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There have been a number of spin-offs from the university's <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">IT</a> technology department.</p>
<p>Aachen is the administrative centre for the coal-mining industries in neighbouring places to the northeast.<sup id="cite_ref-DofA_19-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DofA-19">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Products manufactured in Aachen include electrical goods, textiles, foodstuffs (chocolate and candy), glass, machinery, rubber products, furniture, metal products.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohen_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-59">[54]</a></sup> Also in and around<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="don't want &quot;around.&quot; Want stuff that is in the city. If there is a metro article, &quot;around&quot; can go there (October 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Aachen is the production of chemicals, plastics, cosmetics, and needles and pins.<sup id="cite_ref-AAE_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAE-31">[26]</a></sup> Though once a major player in Aachen's economy, today glassware and textile production make up only 10% of total manufacturing jobs in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-name_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name-11">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_vehicle_manufacturing">Electric vehicle manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Electric vehicle manufacturing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2016-12-10-Post_Streetscooter-9409.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/2016-12-10-Post_Streetscooter-9409.jpg/220px-2016-12-10-Post_Streetscooter-9409.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/2016-12-10-Post_Streetscooter-9409.jpg/330px-2016-12-10-Post_Streetscooter-9409.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/2016-12-10-Post_Streetscooter-9409.jpg/440px-2016-12-10-Post_Streetscooter-9409.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2016-12-10-Post_Streetscooter-9409.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
StreetScooter <i>Work</i> as DHL delivery van (2016)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In June 2010, Achim Kampker, together with Günther Schuh, founded a small company to develop Street Scooter GmbH; in August 2014, it was renamed StreetScooter GmbH. This was a privately organised research initiative at the <a href="/wiki/RWTH_Aachen_University" title="RWTH Aachen University">RWTH Aachen University</a> which later became an independent company in Aachen. Kampker was also the founder and chairman of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Network_for_Affordable_and_Sustainable_Electromobility&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="European Network for Affordable and Sustainable Electromobility (page does not exist)">European Network for Affordable and Sustainable Electromobility</a>. In May 2014, the company announced that the city of Aachen, the city council Aachen and the savings bank Aachen had ordered electric vehicles from the company. In late 2014, approximately 70 employees were manufacturing 200 vehicles annually in the premises of the <a href="/wiki/Waggonfabrik_Talbot" title="Waggonfabrik Talbot">Waggonfabrik Talbot</a>, the former Talbot/Bombardier plant in Aachen.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2014 <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Post" title="Deutsche Post">Deutsche Post DHL Group</a> purchased the StreetScooter company, which became its wholly owned subsidiary.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[65]</a></sup> By April 2016, the company announced that it would produce 2000 of its electric vans branded <i>Work</i> in Aachen by the end of the year.</p>
<p>In April 2016, <a href="/wiki/StreetScooter" title="StreetScooter">StreetScooter</a> GmbH announced that it would be scaling up to manufacture approximately 10,000 of the <i>Work</i> vehicles annually, starting in 2017, also in Aachen.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[66]</a></sup> If that goal is achieved, it will become the largest electric light utility vehicle manufacturer in Europe, surpassing Renault which makes the smaller <i><a href="/wiki/Renault_Kangoo" title="Renault Kangoo">Kangoo Z.E.</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Rosenmontag_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Aachen_Rosenmontag_2009.jpg/220px-Aachen_Rosenmontag_2009.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Aachen_Rosenmontag_2009.jpg/330px-Aachen_Rosenmontag_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Aachen_Rosenmontag_2009.jpg/440px-Aachen_Rosenmontag_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2691" data-file-height="2067" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Rosenmontag_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aachen is also famous for its <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">carnival</a> (Karneval, Fasching), in which families dress in colourful costumes</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1372, Aachen became the first coin-minting city in the world to regularly place an <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">Anno Domini</a> date on a general circulation <a href="/wiki/Coin" title="Coin">coin</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Groschen" title="Groschen">groschen</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Scotch-Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotch-Club">Scotch-Club</a> in Aachen was the first <a href="/wiki/Discoth%C3%A8que" class="mw-redirect" title="Discothèque">discothèque</a>; it has been open since 19 October 1959. Klaus Quirini as DJ Heinrich was the first DJ ever.</p>
<p>The thriving Aachen <a href="/wiki/Black_metal" title="Black metal">black metal</a> scene is among the most notable in Germany, with such bands as <a href="/wiki/Nagelfar" title="Nagelfar">Nagelfar</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Ruins_of_Beverast" title="The Ruins of Beverast">The Ruins of Beverast</a>, Graupel and Verdunkeln.</p>
<p>The local speciality of Aachen is an originally hard type of sweet bread, baked in large flat loaves, called <i><a href="/wiki/Aachener_Printen" title="Aachener Printen">Aachener Printen</a></i>. Unlike <i><a href="/wiki/Lebkuchen" title="Lebkuchen">Lebkuchen</a></i>, a German form of <a href="/wiki/Gingerbread" title="Gingerbread">gingerbread</a> sweetened with honey, <i>Printen</i> use a syrup made from sugar. Today, a soft version is sold under the same name which follows an entirely different recipe.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_RWTH_Hauptgebaeude.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Aachen_RWTH_Hauptgebaeude.jpg/220px-Aachen_RWTH_Hauptgebaeude.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Aachen_RWTH_Hauptgebaeude.jpg/330px-Aachen_RWTH_Hauptgebaeude.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Aachen_RWTH_Hauptgebaeude.jpg/440px-Aachen_RWTH_Hauptgebaeude.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4760" data-file-height="3320" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_RWTH_Hauptgebaeude.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The main building of RWTH Aachen University</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen-ElegantStreet.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aachen-ElegantStreet.JPG/220px-Aachen-ElegantStreet.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aachen-ElegantStreet.JPG/330px-Aachen-ElegantStreet.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Aachen-ElegantStreet.JPG/440px-Aachen-ElegantStreet.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen-ElegantStreet.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typical Aachen street with early 20th-century <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnderzeit" title="Gründerzeit">Gründerzeit</a> houses</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Typical_Aachen_street_with_early_20th-century_Gr%C3%BCnderzeit_houses_(2).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Typical_Aachen_street_with_early_20th-century_Gr%C3%BCnderzeit_houses_%282%29.JPG/220px-Typical_Aachen_street_with_early_20th-century_Gr%C3%BCnderzeit_houses_%282%29.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Typical_Aachen_street_with_early_20th-century_Gr%C3%BCnderzeit_houses_%282%29.JPG/330px-Typical_Aachen_street_with_early_20th-century_Gr%C3%BCnderzeit_houses_%282%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Typical_Aachen_street_with_early_20th-century_Gr%C3%BCnderzeit_houses_%282%29.JPG/440px-Typical_Aachen_street_with_early_20th-century_Gr%C3%BCnderzeit_houses_%282%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1068" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Typical_Aachen_street_with_early_20th-century_Gr%C3%BCnderzeit_houses_(2).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Another example of Aachen early 20th-century Gründerzeit houses</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/RWTH_Aachen" class="mw-redirect" title="RWTH Aachen">RWTH Aachen University</a>, established as Polytechnicum in 1870, is one of <a href="/wiki/German_Universities_Excellence_Initiative" title="German Universities Excellence Initiative">Germany's Universities of Excellence</a> with strong emphasis on technological research, especially for electrical and mechanical engineering, computer sciences, physics, and chemistry. The university clinic attached to the RWTH, the <a href="/wiki/Klinikum_Aachen" class="mw-redirect" title="Klinikum Aachen">Klinikum Aachen</a>, is the biggest single-building hospital in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[68]</a></sup> Over time, a host of software and computer industries have developed around the university. It also maintains a <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_Aachen" title="Botanischer Garten Aachen">Botanischer Garten Aachen</a>).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/FH_Aachen" title="FH Aachen">FH Aachen</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen_University_of_Applied_Sciences&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aachen University of Applied Sciences (page does not exist)">Aachen University of Applied Sciences</a> (AcUAS) was founded in 1971. The AcUAS offers a classic engineering education in professions such as <a href="/wiki/Mechatronics" title="Mechatronics">mechatronics</a>, construction engineering, mechanical engineering or electrical engineering. German and international students are educated in more than 20 international or foreign-oriented programmes and can acquire German as well as international degrees (Bachelor/Master) or <i>Doppelabschlüsse</i> (double degrees). Foreign students account for more than 21% of the student body.</p>
<p>The Katholische Hochschule Nordrhein-Westfalen – Abteilung Aachen (Catholic University of Applied Sciences Northrhine-Westphalia – Aachen department)<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[69]</a></sup> offers its some 750 students a variety of degree programmes: social work, childhood education, nursing, and co-operative management. It also has the only programme of study in Germany especially designed for mothers.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_Musik_und_Tanz_K%C3%B6ln" title="Hochschule für Musik und Tanz Köln">Hochschule für Musik und Tanz Köln</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cologne_University_of_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Cologne University of Music">Cologne University of Music</a>) is one of the world's foremost performing arts schools and one of the largest music institutions for higher education in Europe<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[71]</a></sup> with one of its three campuses in Aachen.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[72]</a></sup> The Aachen campus substantially contributes to the Opera/Musical Theatre master's programme by collaborating with the <a href="/wiki/Theater_Aachen" title="Theater Aachen">Theater Aachen</a> and the recently established musical theatre chair through the Rheinische Opernakademie.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/German_Army" title="German Army">German Army</a>'s Technical School (<i>Ausbildungszentrum Technik Landsysteme</i>) is in Aachen.<sup id="cite_ref-MeerOpitz1998_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MeerOpitz1998-78">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Tivoli_under_construction.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Aachen_Tivoli_under_construction.JPG/220px-Aachen_Tivoli_under_construction.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Aachen_Tivoli_under_construction.JPG/330px-Aachen_Tivoli_under_construction.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Aachen_Tivoli_under_construction.JPG/440px-Aachen_Tivoli_under_construction.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Tivoli_under_construction.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/New_Tivoli" title="New Tivoli">New Tivoli</a>, home ground of <a href="/wiki/Alemannia_Aachen" title="Alemannia Aachen">Alemannia Aachen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The annual CHIO (short for the French term <i>Concours Hippique International Officiel</i>) is the biggest <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> meeting of the world and among horsemen is considered to be as prestigious for equitation as the tournament of <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">Wimbledon</a> for tennis. Aachen hosted the <a href="/wiki/2006_FEI_World_Equestrian_Games" title="2006 FEI World Equestrian Games">2006 FEI World Equestrian Games</a>.</p>
<p>The local <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team <a href="/wiki/Alemannia_Aachen" title="Alemannia Aachen">Alemannia Aachen</a> had a short run-out in Germany's <a href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="Fußball-Bundesliga">first division</a>, after its promotion in 2006. However, the team could not sustain its status and is now back in the fourth division. The stadium <a href="/wiki/Old_Tivoli" title="Old Tivoli">"Tivoli"</a>, opened in 1928, served as the venue for the team's home games and was well known for its incomparable atmosphere throughout the whole of the second division.<sup id="cite_ref-GdawietzLeroi2007_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GdawietzLeroi2007-79">[74]</a></sup> Before the old stadium's demolition in 2011, it was used by amateurs, whilst the Bundesliga Club held its games in the new stadium "Neuer Tivoli" – meaning <a href="/wiki/New_Tivoli" title="New Tivoli">New Tivoli</a>—a couple of metres down the road. The building work for the stadium which has a capacity of 32,960, began in May 2008 and was completed by the beginning of 2009.</p>
<p>The city's biggest tennis club, "TC Grün Weiss", annually hosts the ATP Tournament.</p>
<p>The Ladies in Black women's volleyball team (part of the "PTSV Aachen" sports club since 2013) has played in the first German volleyball league (DVL) since 2008.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aachen's railway station, the <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Aachen Central Station">Hauptbahnhof</a> (Central Station), was constructed in 1841 for the <a href="/wiki/Cologne%E2%80%93Aachen_high-speed_railway" title="Cologne–Aachen high-speed railway">Cologne–Aachen railway line</a>. In 1905 it was moved closer to the city centre. It serves main lines to Cologne, <a href="/wiki/Aachen%E2%80%93M%C3%B6nchengladbach_railway" title="Aachen–Mönchengladbach railway">Mönchengladbach</a> and <a href="/wiki/HSL_3" title="HSL 3">Liège</a> as well as branch lines to <a href="/wiki/Heerlen" title="Heerlen">Heerlen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alsdorf" title="Alsdorf">Alsdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stolberg_(Rhineland)" title="Stolberg (Rhineland)">Stolberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eschweiler" title="Eschweiler">Eschweiler</a>. <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE high speed trains</a> from <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> via <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> trains from Paris to Cologne also stop at Aachen Central Station. Four <a href="/wiki/Regional-Express" title="Regional-Express">RE</a> lines and two <a href="/wiki/Regionalbahn" title="Regionalbahn">RB</a> lines connect Aachen with the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhrgebiet</a>, Mönchengladbach, Spa (Belgium), <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Siegerland" title="Siegerland">Siegerland</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Euregiobahn" title="Euregiobahn">Euregiobahn</a></i>, a regional railway system, reaches several minor cities in the Aachen region.</p>
<p>There are four smaller stations in Aachen: <i><a href="/wiki/Aachen_West_station" title="Aachen West station">Aachen West</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Aachen_Schanz_station" title="Aachen Schanz station">Aachen Schanz</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Aachen-Rothe_Erde_station" title="Aachen-Rothe Erde station">Aachen-Rothe Erde</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Eilendorf_station" title="Eilendorf station">Eilendorf</a></i>. Slower trains stop at these. Aachen West has gained in importance with the expansion of <a href="/wiki/RWTH_Aachen_University" title="RWTH Aachen University">RWTH Aachen University</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OecherLongWajong1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/OecherLongWajong1.JPG/220px-OecherLongWajong1.JPG" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/OecherLongWajong1.JPG/330px-OecherLongWajong1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/OecherLongWajong1.JPG/440px-OecherLongWajong1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3102" data-file-height="2200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OecherLongWajong1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bi-articulated_bus" title="Bi-articulated bus">Bi-articulated bus</a> of the city's transit authority ASEAG, at the <a href="/wiki/Klinikum_Aachen" class="mw-redirect" title="Klinikum Aachen">university hospital</a> bus stop</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first horse tram line in Aachen opened in December 1880. After electrification in 1895, it was with maximal 213.5 kilometres (132.7&#160;mi) in 1915 the fourth-longest tram system in Germany. Many tram lines extended to the surrounding towns of <a href="/wiki/Herzogenrath" title="Herzogenrath">Herzogenrath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stolberg_(Rheinland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stolberg (Rheinland)">Stolberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alsdorf" title="Alsdorf">Alsdorf</a> as well as the Belgian and Dutch communes of <a href="/wiki/Vaals" title="Vaals">Vaals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelmis" title="Kelmis">Kelmis</a> (then <i>Altenberg</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Eupen" title="Eupen">Eupen</a>. The Aachen tram system was linked with the <a href="/wiki/Vicinal_tramway" title="Vicinal tramway">Belgian national interurban tram system</a>. Like many tram systems in Western Europe, the Aachen tram suffered from not well-maintained infrastructure and was so deemed unnecessary and disrupting for car drivers by local politics. On 28 September 1974 the last line 15 (Vaals–Brand) operated for one last day and was then replaced by buses. A proposal to reinstate a tram/light rail system under the name <i>Campusbahn</i> was dropped after a referendum.</p>
<p>Today, the ASEAG (<i>Aachener Straßenbahn und Energieversorgungs-AG</i>, literally "Aachen tram and power supply company") operates an 1,240.8 kilometres (771.0&#160;mi) long bus network with 68 bus routes. Because of the location at the border, many bus routes extend to Belgium and the Netherlands. Lines 14 to Eupen, Belgium and 44 to Heerlen, Netherlands are jointly operated with <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_R%C3%A9gionale_Wallonne_du_Transport" title="Société Régionale Wallonne du Transport">Transport en Commun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veolia_Transport_Nederland" title="Veolia Transport Nederland">Veolia Transport Nederland</a>, respectively. ASEAG is one of the main participants in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachener_Verkehrsverbund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aachener Verkehrsverbund (page does not exist)">Aachener Verkehrsverbund</a>, a tariff association in the region.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aachen is connected to the <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a> <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_4" title="Bundesautobahn 4">A4</a> (West-East), <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_44" title="Bundesautobahn 44">A44</a> (North-South) and A544 (a smaller motorway from the A4 to the <i>Europaplatz</i> near the city centre). There are plans to eliminate traffic jams at the Aachen road interchange.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Aachen_Airport" title="Maastricht Aachen Airport">Maastricht Aachen Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" class="mw-redirect" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>MST</b>,&#160;<a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" class="mw-redirect" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EHBK</b>) is the main airport of Aachen and <a href="/wiki/Maastricht" title="Maastricht">Maastricht</a>. It is located around 15 NM (28&#160;km; 17&#160;mi) northwest of Aachen. There is a shuttle-service between Aachen and the airport.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Charlemagne_Prize">Charlemagne Prize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Charlemagne Prize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne_Prize" title="Charlemagne Prize">Charlemagne Prize</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angela_Merkel,_Karlspreisverleihung_2008_-_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Angela_Merkel%2C_Karlspreisverleihung_2008_-_1.jpg/180px-Angela_Merkel%2C_Karlspreisverleihung_2008_-_1.jpg" width="180" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Angela_Merkel%2C_Karlspreisverleihung_2008_-_1.jpg/270px-Angela_Merkel%2C_Karlspreisverleihung_2008_-_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Angela_Merkel%2C_Karlspreisverleihung_2008_-_1.jpg/360px-Angela_Merkel%2C_Karlspreisverleihung_2008_-_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1336" data-file-height="1931" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Angela_Merkel,_Karlspreisverleihung_2008_-_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">Chancellor of Germany</a> <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>, wearing the Charlemagne Prize awarded to her in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1950, a committee of Aachen citizens annually awards the Charlemagne Prize (German: <span lang="de">Karlspreis</span>) to personalities of outstanding service to the unification of Europe. It is traditionally awarded on <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Ascension Day">Ascension Day</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Rathaus" title="Aachen Rathaus">City Hall</a>. In 2016, the Charlemagne Award was awarded to <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a>.</p>
<p>The International Charlemagne Prize of Aachen was awarded in the year 2000 to US president <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, for his special personal contribution to co-operation with the states of Europe, for the preservation of peace, freedom, democracy and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Europe" title="Human rights in Europe">human rights in Europe</a>, and for his support of the enlargement of the European Union. In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a>'s efforts to unite Europe were honoured with an "Extraordinary Charlemagne Medal", which was awarded for the only time ever.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aachen is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:<sup id="cite_ref-en-db_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en-db-80">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Calderdale_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calderdale-81">[76]</a></sup></p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington County, Virginia</a>, US (1993)<sup id="cite_ref-Calderdale_81-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calderdale-81">[76]</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aachen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"RWTH" is the abbreviation of "Rheinisch-Westfälische Technische Hochschule", which translates into "Rhine-Westphalian Technical University". The institution is commonly referred to as "RWTH Aachen" or simply "RWTH", with the abbreviation remaining untranslated in other languages to avoid the use of the "Hochschule" term, which is sometimes mistakenly translated as <a href="/wiki/High_school_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="High school (disambiguation)">high school</a>. Sometimes, RWTH Aachen is also referred to as "TH Aachen" or "Aachen University". However, the term "FH Aachen" does not refer to the RWTH but to the <a href="/wiki/Fachhochschule_Aachen" class="mw-redirect" title="Fachhochschule Aachen">Fachhochschule Aachen</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Fachhochschule" title="Fachhochschule">university of applied sciences</a>, which is also in Aachen.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This audio file is Andreas Schaub explaining the archaeological record in court in <i>Archäologie am Hof</i>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is in dispute, as some history books state that Charlemagne was in fact born in Aachen in 742.<sup id="cite_ref-WB_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB-23">[21]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This was between 970 and 980.<sup id="cite_ref-dupuy_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dupuy-26">[23]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sources differ on the age of the <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Rathaus" title="Aachen Rathaus">city hall</a>, as the dates used for the construction were 1334–1349.<sup id="cite_ref-DofA_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DofA-19">[17]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
